        <p class="date">
         Mon Jun 23, 2014 at 11:14 AM PDT
        </p>
        <h2>
         <a href="/story/2014/06/23/1308997/-The-Humanitarian-Left" id="titleHref">
          The Humanitarian Left
         </a>
         <span style="white-space: nowrap">
         </span>
        </h2>
        <p class="author">
         <span>
          by
         </span>
         <a href="/user/One Pissed Off Liberal">
          One Pissed Off Liberal
         </a>
         <a alt="Follow this author" class="ajax type-user do-hotlist do-updateContent size-tiny off altTooltip" href="#?friend_id=85446&amp;is_stream=1">
          Follow
         </a>
        </p>
        <ul class="front-page-share clearfix">
         <li style="margin-left: 0px">
          <div class="fb-share-button" data-href="http://www.dailykos.com/story/2014/06/23/1308997/-The-Humanitarian-Left" data-layout="button_count">
          </div>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a class="twitter-share-button" data-count="horizontal" data-related="markos" data-text="The Humanitarian Left" data-url="http://www.dailykos.com/story/2014/06/23/1308997/-The-Humanitarian-Left" data-via="dailykos" href="https://twitter.com/share">
           Tweet
          </a>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a class="comments comment_count_with_new" data-comment_count="160" data-story_id="1308997" href="/story/2014/06/23/1308997/-The-Humanitarian-Left#comments">
           160 Comments
          </a>
         </li>
        </ul>
       </div>
       <div class="article-body">
        <div id="intro">
         <blockquote>
          <strong>
           Note
          </strong>
          : This article is cross-posted from
          <a href="http://www.humanitarianleft.com/">
           Humanitarian Left
          </a>
          .
         </blockquote>
         I think of myself as being part of the humanitarian left. That's not a formal thing (afaik). I'm not an ideologue, a dedicated Marxist or committed socialist (though I do lean that way). I just come down on the left side of things because that's where one finds compassion, charity, kindness, altruism, etc.- all those things that I perceive to be the best of which we are capable. I define myself as a leftist in opposition to what one finds on the right: selfishness, greed, profits over people, authoritarian meanness, police-state regulation of the powerless and lawlessness for the rich and powerful. It's easy to be selfish and mean, perhaps that's why so many people are. It's much harder, and more laudatory in my view, to be a humanitarian. After all, what does the world need more of? Mean, selfish, greedy assholes? Or humanitarians? I think the answer is obvious.
        </div>
        <p class="divider-doodle">
        </p>
        <div class="article-body" id="body">
         <p>
          Like I say, I'm no communist but my sympathies definitely lie with:
         </p>
         <p>
          The unemployed
          <br/>
          The under-employed
          <br/>
          The under-paid
          <br/>
          The unfortunate
          <br/>
          The downtrodden
          <br/>
          The oppressed
          <br/>
          The imprisoned
          <br/>
          The homeless
          <br/>
          The discriminated against
          <br/>
          The suffering masses
         </p>
         <p>
          If that makes me a commie in your book, so be it. What
          <strong>
           I
          </strong>
          think I am is a humanitarian.
         </p>
         <p>
          I realize that my left/right characterization is simplistic and that it's not all that black and white, that the issues are many-layered and complex. That's just a quick and crude summary of my personal view of it. Apologies to compassionate conservatives, should there be any, or well-meaning centrists.
         </p>
         <p>
          Also, apologies to doctrinaire or academic leftists who might prefer a more orthodox approach to the language of the left. While I want to be informed by history always, science and truth as well, I want to take only what is most useful from old ideologies and be flexible and thoughtful about meeting our unprecedented challenges. I'm the Bruce Lee of armchair philosophers (I suppose only martial artists will get that reference): I believe in taking from here and from there what is of use and discarding the rest. I think we need to be thoughtful, open-minded, eclectic and practical while embracing compassion and cooperation as we seek new ways forward to a new world. Forward is the operative word. It's time for humanity to advance while it still can. I don't think the prescription for our ills has yet been written. We have to do it ourselves. And we have to be massively creative. We need to rethink and re-imagine everything. We need to see with new eyes.
         </p>
         <p>
          I'm for the nanny state, though I prefer 'the nurturing state.' 'The Nanny State' is of course rightwing propaganda to make helping each other seem bad. If we were preoccupied with helping each other out, we might stop slaughtering each other and quit obsessing over militarism, conquest and thievery.
         </p>
         <p>
          From the very beginnings of humanity, we survived as a species precisely and only because we are a social species  because we are capable of intelligence, cooperation, compassion and altruism. As relatively vulnerable members of the animal kingdom, those are really our only advantages.
         </p>
         <p>
          Being as how we
          <strong>
           are
          </strong>
          a social species, I believe we have solemn responsibilities to one another. I believe it is our duty to take proper care of each other. Why wouldn't it be? What else is a society good for? While I may not be a pure socialist, since I believe that one can draw from a variety of philosophies and that the complexity of the modern world demands that sort of flexibility, I believe that Medicine, Banking and Energy, at a minimum, should be socialized. Making these important social functions profit centers for capitalist cowboys has been a horrible mistake. Some things don't work as capitalist toys. Some things are too important to be played with. Prisons for example. That we ever evolved for-profit prisons is a measure of how much we as a nation have lost our soul.
         </p>
         <p>
          I find the current state of the U.S. political system appalling, aggravating, unhelpful and unacceptable. I tend to see it as a big roiling stew of backstabbing opportunists, dueling egos, greedheads and power-whores vying for the spoils in a giant lying contest, all the while sitting on go to sell us all out in a heartbeat. It serves no useful purpose whatsoever, as far as I can tell, other than to keep the people distracted and to protect and advance the short-sighted interests of the greed-deranged one percent while stymieing progressive change. But I'm not one of those who think we need smaller government. I think we need better government. Smarter government. This mind-numbingly dumb government is going to kill us all.
         </p>
         <p>
          As far as politicians go, I support reformers and only reformers. No one who perpetuates, enables or props up the present con job of a system is worthy of support, in my view. More of the same is no longer a viable option. What we need is change, deep-running, thorough, no bullshit change. And damn the next person who promises it dishonestly.
         </p>
         <p>
          Our best and brightest began to see, as far back as the 50s or 60s, that our management of the present and plans for the future left much to be desired and required a major tweak or two, that we would not get much further without evolving into a more sustainable way of life. Emergent humanity got a few things wrong with respect to long term planning, as it turns out, and it has long been time for an adjustment, a major shifting of the gears, to a new, more comprehensive understanding of humanity's relationship to the earth, the cosmos and each other.
         </p>
         <p>
          It's time to rethink the way we do things: poisoning the environment and destroying the soil with our bone-headed approach to agriculture, mindlessly gobbling up precious resources, burning fossil fuels, polluting the environment, laying waste the ecosphere, ignoring the voracious character of our competitive/capitalist/consumerist way of life while stubbornly refusing to acknowledge the existence of environmental limitations or the ravages thus far wreaked.
         </p>
         <p>
          Sane people who were paying attention have long seen how desperately we need to change if are going to make it as a species. Conservatives have fought any and all efforts to change anything for the better every step of the way. They liked things just as they were. Their greed blinded them and caused a knee-jerk doubling down on the bad bet the status quo portended. They've nearly won the battle for no change at all too. Their victory? The doom of the many, the triumph of the aggressively dumb and catastrophic loss to all.
         </p>
         <p>
          The saddest part of this history is how the supposed liberals, the politicians anyway, threw in with conservatives to stymie change and prop up the loathsome status quo because there was more money in carrying water for the stupid-rich psychopaths than representing the interests of ordinary people. Not that it happened all at once or out in the open. But happen it did.
         </p>
         <p>
          We simply can't go on in this manner. Einstein said the same thinking that brought us here won't get us out. Tweaking the current system is an inadequate response to present realities. We need to rethink everything. We need to de-construct/reconstruct the socio-political mechanisms by which we make policy and address issues. The special interests and the Big Money crowd need to butt the fuck out. The Military Industrial Complex needs to be repurposed, actual defense matters put in a box appropriately sized to meet actual threats, while we go about the business of defusing the planet and rescuing the ecosphere.
         </p>
         <p>
          I wouldn't recommend changing American values one iota. I'd love to see us get back to them  or rather come to them in a genuine way for the first time ever. It's time to re-implement the Bill of Rights. It's time again for equality and liberty, freedom of speech and press, and justice for all.
         </p>
         <p>
          But fa realz, this time.
         </p>
         <p>
          And no more rich folk whining about taxes. The wealth of a society should be used to make that society whole and healthy...for all its members.
         </p>
         <p>
          If you're a rich person, you are one of the luckiest people on the planet, indeed one of the luckiest people in all history, and you have a social obligation to give back. That's what it is to live in a society. That's what it means to be a member of a social species. You don't get to be nurtured and made rich by a society and the opportunities it provides and then ignore it and disavow any responsibility to it once you're a success. No, you did not build that, not alone you didn't, not in a vacuum you didn't. Enough with the myth of the self-made man. Those who succeed do so within the context of a nurturing society that provides the infrastructure, the support, the stability and the tools that make success possible. We all depend on each other. That's the way societies work. The myth of the rugged individualist is just that, a myth. Success should be spread from the top to the bottom. That way all members of the society are nurtured...as it should be. What's the point in even having a society, a civilization, a tribe, a family if it's every-man-for-himself? Dog-eat-dog is no way to run a civilization. We are not savages. Except when we choose to be. But why would we?
         </p>
         <p>
          Why do we?
         </p>
         <p>
          We need to embark on a new era of global cooperation. Earthlings, a threatened species, need to have a big group hug. Our survival depends upon it. Our obsession with competition, ruthless murderous competition, is killing the planet and our species. I pray that we are not stupid enough to keep doing this.
         </p>
         <p>
          Only by unprecedented international cooperation will humanity stand a chance at a reasonable future.
         </p>
         <p>
          We're going to have to turn this ship around and start doing the right things. We're going to have to stop wasting time and treasure on made-up conflicts and petty squabbles while doing nothing to preserve and protect the rainforests and all the other dwindling natural resources. We're going to have to stop doing nothing about climate change, and start observing all the finite planetary limits we've been pretending don't exist. We're going to have to change our ways, and profoundly so.
         </p>
         <p>
          We need to remake our institutions so that they are responsive to the people and useful to the species.
         </p>
         <p>
          We're going to have to stop burning fossil fuels, poisoning the land, sea, air and water. We're going to have to stop squabbling, fighting and playing king-of-the-hill.
         </p>
         <p>
          We have to overcome our hatreds and fears. We have to stop killing and waging war on each other. These are significant challenges, of course, but they are imperatives. If we don't set out to do these things, they won't get done. The money we mindlessly waste on militarism could rescue our planet and provide healthcare, food, renewable energy and water for all.
         </p>
         <p>
          We need to start conserving energy, food, medicine and water. We need to reform our distribution systems so that the hungry are fed, the ill tended to and people have all the potable water they need. We need to stop spraying poisons, polluting the environment, causing erosion and wasting precious resources. We need to stop the needless consumption of meaningless goods, cheap plastic crap and mindless propaganda and start living as if it truly matters. We need to find ways to live meaningfully, intelligently and mindfully.
         </p>
         <p>
          We must take all possible steps to alleviate human suffering to the fullest extent possible and preserve a healthy and viable ecosphere for future generations. Our failure to do this is a failure indeed.
         </p>
         <p>
          We must quit repeating past mistakes and stop doing all the stupid things that only promise doom. We need to make a good faith effort to live up to the moniker with which we've so humbly crowned ourselves: homo sapiens sapiens - wise or knowing man.
         </p>
         <p>
          It's time for our species to grow up.
         </p>
         <p>
          If we are truly as wise as I hope we are, as I suspect we may be, as I pray we are - we are going to finally make world peace and save the species.
         </p>
         <p>
          May it come to pass.
         </p>
         <p>
          Selah.
          <br/>
         </p>
         <blockquote>
          <strong>
           P.S.
          </strong>
          My son, the bodhisattva, made me a website for father's day. It's a modest little thing, but pretty cool for a one-man effort. With a little love it could grow into something truly worthwhile. That's what we're hoping for. We'd love it if you'd drop by for a visit. We need beta testers, writers and community support. It's called
          <a href="http://www.humanitarianleft.com/">
           Humanitarian Left
          </a>
          .
         </blockquote>
         <img alt="Playa-Chiquita-Peace-Out" height="420" src="http://farm8.staticflickr.com/7459/13389831514_ebf4856564_o.jpg" width="560"/>
        </div>
       </div>

         <div class="tooltipContents qtip-style-dk4_large qtip-pos-br">
          <p>
           <b>
            More Tagging tips:
           </b>
          </p>
          <p>
           A tag is a way to search for this diary. If someone is searching for "Barack Obama," is this a diary they'd be trying to find?
          </p>
          <p>
           Use a person's full name, without any title. Senator Obama may become President Obama, and Michelle Obama might run for office.
          </p>
          <p>
           If your diary covers an election or elected official, use election tags, which are generally the state abbreviation followed by the office. 
		CA-01 is the first district House seat. CA-Sen covers both senate races. NY-GOV covers the New York governor's race.
          </p>
          <p>
           Tags do not compound: that is, "education reform" is a completely different tag from "education". A tag like "reform" alone is probably not meaningful.
          </p>
         </div>

          <li id="c133">
           <div class="cx" id="cx53766919">
            <h5>
             <a class="de">
             </a>
             <span class="cu">
              The difference between a humanitarian
             </span>
             <span class="crd ntb">
              (
              <a href="/comments/1308997/53766919#c133?mode=alone;showrate=1#c133">
               2+ / 0-
              </a>
              )
             </span>
            </h5>
            <div class="crs">
             <dl>
              <dt>
               Recommended by:
              </dt>
              <dd>
               <a href="/user/uid:973366">
                acornweb
               </a>
               ,
               <a href="/user/uid:983613">
                Prickly Pam
               </a>
              </dd>
             </dl>
            </div>
            <div class="ct">
             <p>
              and a liberal is who gets to pay the bill. In my opinion, a humanitarian gives their own time and money.
             </p>
             <p>
              Much as I want to help others and fix the world, I've known too many people who won't voter for Democrats because our social welfare systems are too easily abused.
             </p>
             <p>
              Maybe we should take a good hard look at how to convert our support systems from handouts to a hand up.
             </p>
             <p>
              (Yes, I know corporate welfare is worse than low level abuse. I want to fix both.)
             </p>
            </div>
            <div class="cf">
             <p class="sig">
             </p>
             <p class="cb">

              <a href="/user/uid:142061">

           <li id="c152">
            <div class="cx" id="cx53786387">
             <h5>
              <a class="de">
              </a>
              <span class="cu">
               when did Liberal stop meaning
              </span>
              <span class="crd ntb">
               (
               <a href="/comments/1308997/53786387#c152?mode=alone;showrate=1#c152">
                1+ / 0-
               </a>
               )
              </span>
             </h5>
             <div class="crs">
              <dl>
               <dt>
                Recommended by:
               </dt>
               <dd>
                <a href="/user/uid:85446">
                 One Pissed Off Liberal
                </a>
               </dd>
              </dl>
             </div>
             <div class="ct">
              <p>
               generous? When did it become a 'dirty word'?
               <br/>
               Let's have some fun with Christian Conservative bible-thumpers and ask every politician who insists this country should be following scripture to implement the commands in Leviticus 25:8-13! Debts forgiven, prisoners freed, foreclosed homes go back to the owners... even the land gets a break from being farmed!
               <br/>
               Yeah... the day they do that we better keep an eye on the thermometer in Hell!
              </p>
             </div>
             <div class="cf">
              <p class="sig">
              </p>
              <p class="cb">
               by
               <a href="/user/uid:986399">
                Kayette
               </a>

           <li id="c155">
            <div class="cx" id="cx53795169">
             <h5>
              <a class="de">
              </a>
              <span class="cu">
               How is it that you think you "know" this?
              </span>
              <span class="crd ntb">
               (
               <a href="/comments/1308997/53795169#c155?mode=alone;showrate=1#c155">
                1+ / 0-
               </a>
               )
              </span>
             </h5>
             <div class="crs">
              <dl>
               <dt>
                Recommended by:
               </dt>
               <dd>
                <a href="/user/uid:85446">
                 One Pissed Off Liberal
                </a>
               </dd>
              </dl>
             </div>
             <div class="ct">
              <p>
               I am wondering if you have ever gone through the process to get food stamps, Medicaid, TAMF or any other social welfare program? Or are you just believing the rightists when they say all the poor, or a lot of the poor, are cheating?
              </p>
              <p>
               People come into my office all the time and complain about how the illegal Mexcians get benefits they, as white working people can't get. I have yet to hear of any actual cases. I think it's a meme started by Ronald Reagan and carried on to this day.
              </p>
              <p>
               Of course there are cheaters, but I think they tend to be large organizations that, for instance, defraud Medicare or Medicaid. And corporate welfare and the war profiteers take far more money than some economically disadvantaged folks who lie on their applications about something. The take home from social welfare programs is pretty darn minimal. Check it out. Look at what the payments are in your county and state, and see if you could make do on that amount. Then look at how many billions the wealthy have in tax havens and rollover setups. Think a little harder and look a little deeper.
              </p>
             </div>

              <p class="sig">

               <a href="/user/uid:37179">
                wordwraith
               </a>
               ,
               <a href="/user/uid:100037">
                US Blues
               </a>
               ,
               <a href="/user/uid:75313">
                PapaChach
               </a>
               ,
               <a href="/user/uid:180755">
                Plox
               </a>
               ,
               <a href="/user/uid:141635">
                greengemini
               </a>
               ,
               <a href="/user/uid:120316">
                CenFlaDem
               </a>
               ,
               <a href="/user/uid:52737">
                ChemBob
               </a>
               ,
               <a href="/user/uid:934178">
                Choco8
               </a>
              </dd>
             </dl>
            </div>
            <div class="ct">
             <p>
              is esp. on point. We both grew up in a country in which it was broadly understood that there were certain public goods--e.g. schools, prisons, hospitals, roads, sewers, water--that should not be governed by the profit motive. There was a widely accepted dividing line between, say, manufacturing cars and educating kids.
             </p>
             <p>
              We've now had over 3 decades in which the very concept of public goods has been under steady assault.  Health care, education, corrections, highways--these are all just another way for connected investors to turn a quick $.  One party believes in this concept w/ religious fervor, while the other, as often as not goes along out of political expediency and/or in search of campaign $.
             </p>
             <p>
              A lot of good Dems over a lot of years built a thriving public sector that met human needs and developed loyalty to the party. That legacy is now virtually forgotten. The abandonment of that legacy has been a boon to the GOP and a detriment to millions of potential Dem voters.
             </p>
            </div>
            <div class="cf">
             <p class="sig">
              Some men see things as they are and ask why.  I dream of things that never were and ask why not?
             </p>
             <p class="cb">
              by
              <a href="/user/uid:15772">
               RFK Lives
              </a>
              on
              <a href="/comments/1308997/53755580#c41">
               Mon Jun 23, 2014 at 01:24:43 PM PDT
              </a>
             </p>
             <p class="cl">

              </a>
              ]
             </p>
            </div>

          <div class="cx" id="cx53759525">
           <h5>
            <a class="de">
            </a>
            <span class="cu">
             Yes &amp; No, Big Al...
            </span>
            <span class="crd ntb">
             (
             <a href="/comments/1308997/53759525#c91?mode=alone;showrate=1#c91">
              8+ / 0-
             </a>
             )
            </span>
           </h5>
           <div class="crs">
            <dl>
             <dt>
              Recommended by:
             </dt>
             <dd>
              <a href="/user/uid:85446">
               One Pissed Off Liberal
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:142311">
               BigAlinWashSt
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:169685">
               Betty Pinson
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:166438">
               gulfgal98
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:166753">
               Lady Libertine
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:29894">
               kharma
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:1008411">
               snwflk
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:1012915">
               cowdab
              </a>
             </dd>
            </dl>
           </div>
           <div class="ct">
            <blockquote>
             Maybe that's just human nature, maybe we're destined to be no more than a colony of ants.
            </blockquote>
            We humans, with our great abilities and inventiveness, have taken the Awesome primal powers of the universe into our hands, it is therefore mandated that we evolve a comparable level of human consciousness, an ethical, moral consciousness which manifests and acts from the one quality fundamental to ALL religions---Compassion.
            <p>
             We may not make it. We may end up as just another withered branch on the great tree of evolution, we may end up as just another 'colony of ants.' But I believe the choice is ours as the next mandated challenge of evolution. It is what our ancestors, and what indigenous people knew and lived.
            </p>
            <p>
             It is for us to make conscious return to these values so we can then use in a positive way, the incredible powers we have attained in technology.
            </p>
            <p>
             Einstein was not kidding when he said that everything had changed "save man's way of thinking." Ergo: the mandate!
            </p>
            <p>
             We must change our thinking.
            </p>
           </div>

         <li id="c108">
          <div class="cx" id="cx53760927">
           <h5>
            <a class="de">
            </a>
            <span class="cu">
             Agroecology, agroforestry and
            </span>
            <span class="crd ntb">
             (
             <a href="/comments/1308997/53760927#c108?mode=alone;showrate=1#c108">
              3+ / 0-
             </a>
             )
            </span>
           </h5>
           <div class="crs">
            <dl>
             <dt>
              Recommended by:
             </dt>
             <dd>
              <a href="/user/uid:85446">
               One Pissed Off Liberal
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:52737">
               ChemBob
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:321609">
               JayRaye
              </a>
             </dd>
            </dl>
           </div>
           <div class="ct">
            <p>
             a similar approach (more hands off) to marine ecosystems can sustain our population better than the current system.
            </p>
            <p>
             Asking whether permaculture can provide for everyone is a bit silly. Permaculture is an ethical design framework. People can choose to use it or not, I don't really care (and this is coming from the person who has tagged permaculture more often on this blog, since Jan 2011, than anyone else).
            </p>
            <p>
             What I care about is the implementation of regenerative land use practices, like those recommended in the UN's Trade and Environment Review 2013 (
             <a href="http://www.dailykos.com/story/2013/10/06/1243242/-Agroecology-Wake-up-before-it-is-too-late-UNCTAD-s-TER13-Report">
              that I blogged about here)
             </a>
             .
            </p>
            <p>
             <a href="http://www.dailykos.com/story/2013/04/18/1198024/-Introduction-to-Agroecology-Green-Gold-The-Source-of-Wealth-is-are-the-Functional-Ecosystems">
              In this diary
             </a>
             you can see how degraded landscapes can be restored to functionality (with the caveat that we can only restore with what we have left- which puts an even greater emphasis on preventing extinction of any species). I think the five plus million Chinese who are living in an appreciating environment now due to a massive publics works project to halt and reverse the centuries long degradation of the Loess Plateau would beg to differ that agroecology and agroforestry cannot sustain our population.
            </p>
            <p>
             How to get from our current system that is, by all accounts, putting us on the express track to catastrophe, begins when enough people who care begin to explore what we already know is possible.
            </p>
            <p>
             The fact of the matter is that we have the know how, we have the means, we have everything we need to reverse just about every problem humanity has created over the past 10,000 years of continuous settlement. What we don't have is the will. And the will will not come if people continue to say it isn't possible in the face of all the evidence that, in fact, it is possible to radically alter our relationship with this planet and help heal the wounds we have caused.
            </p>
           </div>
           <div class="cf">
            <p class="sig">
             <a href="http://finchj9b.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow">
              A Victory Garden
             </a>
             documents my family's lawn to edible food forest transition.
             <a href="http://60npermaculture.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow">
              60 N Permaculture explores my life as an expat in Finland.
             </a>
            </p>
            <p class="cb">
             by
             <a href="/user/uid:146565">
              FinchJ
             </a>
             on
             <a href="/comments/1308997/53760927#c108">
              Tue Jun 24, 2014 at 04:54:46 AM PDT
             </a>
            </p>
            <p class="cl">
             [
             <a href="#c32">
              Parent
             </a>
             ]
            </p>
           </div>
          </div>

              0+ / 0-
             </a>
             )
            </span>
           </h5>
           <div class="ct">
            <p>
             Some pretty smart heads are predicting a 70% reduction in the agricultural output of the USA this century due to climate change (RISKY BUSINESS: The Economic Risks of Climate Change in the United States). No food; no people.
             <br/>
             Sidenote.... The principles in that report read like a Who's Who of Ayn Rand's priesthood.
             <br/>
             Bottom line.... The high priests of self aggrandizement are starting to get seriously worried. But don't feel sorry for them. They are smart enough to know when to short which stocks and make piles of money.
             <br/>
            </p>

          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            centers. It is very upsetting that the delivery of fresh water is now becoming another service that local governments are selling off. Services like that become much more expensive when there is a need to generate a profit for the CEOs and the investor class.
           </p>
           <p>
            We can't all be millionaires, and life isn't fair. But we can decide to make life more fair. With the wealth in our nation we could easily provide a roof for everyone and enough calories to keep people's mind and spirits working. There's nothing wrong with being rich, unless you got that way by taking advantage of your employees and customers.

        <li id="c66">
         <div class="cx" id="cx53756531">
          <h5>
           <a class="de">
           </a>
           <span class="cu">
            On the Left/Right stuff, just read an article
           </span>
           <span class="crd ntb">
            (
            <a href="/comments/1308997/53756531#c66?mode=alone;showrate=1#c66">
             14+ / 0-
            </a>
            )
           </span>
          </h5>
          <div class="crs">
           <dl>
            <dt>
             Recommended by:
            </dt>
            <dd>
             <a href="/user/uid:85446">
              One Pissed Off Liberal
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:166438">
              gulfgal98
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:107837">
              on the cusp
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:56833">
              Burned
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:198313">
              tardis10
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:142311">
              BigAlinWashSt
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:252480">
              peachcreek
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:45698">
              3goldens
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:163287">
              janis b
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:650205">
              jbsoul
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:57293">
              lotlizard
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:98722">
              aliasalias
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:29894">
              kharma
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:52737">
              ChemBob
             </a>
            </dd>
           </dl>
          </div>
          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            (at
            <em>
             The Atlantic
            </em>
            was it?) which said useful things, not the least of them the incoherence of what we are told are Conservative/Liberal, Republican/Democratic policies.
           </p>
           <p>
            My grasp of it: The whole 'is it Money or Government' which one should favor is pretty meaningless in real life. The barrier between them is, always has been, just a theoretical construct. The Power flows between them and you don't really get Big Business or Big Government without one helping the other get that way.
           </p>
           <p>
            Look at cable, or utilities, for instance: We live here with effective monopolies on each, where there was a government deal with the companies to build the infrastructure in return for getting the customers. We see that every regulatory agency gets captured by the industry it's supposed to regulate. And then with the funds the cable company, the pharma company, makes, they buy politicians who write rules that protect the industries and discourage competition.
           </p>
           <p>
            And of course, there's War, as the perfect example of the Government/Business alliance.
           </p>
           <p>
            The author thought the more meaningful frame by which to judge a thing's value is whether a given law or policy creates or weakens hierarchies. Which makes sense to me.
           </p>
           <p>
            The Left/Right thing, as far as I can tell, leads to some advantages to people at the margins (as little as politically feasible), but allows the key decisions to remain in the hands of the elites. Elites who overlap, or rotate, in function as to whether they are nominally about Money or Government.
           </p>
           <p>
            We can definitely say that the hyper-version of Conservative/Liberal the media feeds us, and conditions us into, is more about divide-and-conquer the People than it is about having a sane society.
           </p>
           <p>
            As to Humanitarian Left: I'm with that. To my mind the world of Real Politics -- not the crap we're told by media, political sophisticates, or schooling -- is about "Sane Informed Adult with Good Intent vs. Narcissistic, Ignorant, Manipulators of Devious Intent" and not much more is needed to understand politics-as-lived.
            <br/>
           </p>
          </div>
          <div class="cf">
           <p class="sig">
           </p>

          </div>
          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            and
            <i>
             your words of wisdom
            </i>
            .
           </p>
           <p>
            This year is my own foray into the arena of "feed yourself", we now have two indoor growing areas (one is a new building, and still needs it's siding and electric wiring) and a 20 x 16 x 12 foot steel-framed outdoor greenhouse (for seeds, early spring shoots and year round herbs and specialties.
           </p>
           <p>
            I have about 1/2 acre of pasture which is getting fruit and nut trees this fall.
           </p>
           <p>
            I'm getting the neighbor's old chicken coop and we're gonna be raising our own meat and eggs.
           </p>
           <p>
            There are family owned and operated dairies within 20 min drive and I'm going to start buying fresh whole milk with cream, so that I can make my own butter. I did it 20 some years ago. You just scoop the cream off, add a bit of salt, put it in a glass canning jar &amp; screw the lid on - and
            <i>
             gently
            </i>
            rock that butter into existence during an evening of tv watching.
           </p>
           <p>
            I'd get a pig, but I have a rule: we don't eat anything with a name. It's not vegan or vegetarian, but it's my own moral line in the sand. We don't eat people, and if you have a name? You's
            <i>
             people
            </i>
            of some sort, to me and mine. Pigs are cute and funny and smart. It sucks that they are also so darned tasty. But if we raised one? It would get a name, I'd probably be the one to name it. So that's out, if I ever hope to eat another bite of ham or bacon (although I've been eating turkey bacon for years now instead of pork).
           </p>
           <p>
            So what I'm trying to say is that I'm on route to building my own little
            <i>
             garden of Eden
            </i>
            here in the exurbs/suburbs of Southwest Washington.
           </p>
           <p>
            I'm hoping to really start getting it going later this fall, as my income rises with current products.
           </p>
           <p>
            I'll be sure to come see ur new digs online, too. After all, how long can a kossack go without an infusion of
            <b>
             OPOL
            </b>
            once in a while, eh?
           </p>
           <p>
            #LLAP
            <br/>
            angie
           </p>

          </div>
          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            like you came back with a renewed sense of purpose and strength. I think it's always beneficial to experience new territory. It provides a unique perspective on the familiar, and some quite surprising insights. I know that the thoughts and understanding you express here in this diary are ones that have always been closest to your heart, and I'm really happy that you have decided to build upon them at your new site. I look forward to reading and participating.
           </p>

         <div class="cx" id="cx53758246">
          <h5>
           <a class="de">
           </a>
           <span class="cu">
            Communism is basically extreme socialism
           </span>
           <span class="crd ntb">
            (
            <a href="/comments/1308997/53758246#c76?mode=alone;showrate=1#c76">
             9+ / 0-
            </a>
            )
           </span>
          </h5>
          <div class="crs">
           <dl>
            <dt>
             Recommended by:
            </dt>
            <dd>
             <a href="/user/uid:321609">
              JayRaye
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:85446">
              One Pissed Off Liberal
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:163287">
              janis b
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:650205">
              jbsoul
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:144846">
              dharmasyd
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:1017558">
              Whamadoodle
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:94755">
              FishOutofWater
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:29894">
              kharma
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:52737">
              ChemBob
             </a>
            </dd>
           </dl>
          </div>
          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            enforced by a few over the many without the latter's consent, and is thus a certain kind of totalitarianism. Socialism, which encompasses a broad and complex spectrum of economic policies (which includes our own), is imposed legislatively by a popularly elected government, and can be reversed, and thus cannot be totalitarian, no matter how much some people whine about it and scream "Communism!". Complete socialism is probably unworkable, as well as unnecessary, and politically untenable. But some form of socialism is essential for any society to thrive and endure. Some aspects of economic activity not only benefit from, but require, being socialized, i.e. involuntarily pooled, e.g. basic infrastructure, schools, police, fire, defense, etc. Other don't "require" it, but greatly benefit from it, like health care and retirement insurance.
           </p>
           <p>
            There really isn't a serious debate to be had on this. We won, on points at least. It's the PR and political battle that we've yet to fully win. We will.
           </p>
          </div>

            <p>
             Also, it helps to keep in mind that Socialism is an economic system and Communism is an ideology which supports socialism as an economic system (political economy.)
            </p>
            <p>
             There are also Christian Socialist, and other ideologies and cultures which endorse Socialism. I worked with a Native-American women in Minneapolis who was not at all bothered when she learned that I was a Socialist, because, she said, she was an Indian and "Indians have always practiced Socialism." (If I remember right she was from the Red Lake Reservation in MN, not far from where I was born and raised.
            </p>
            <p>
             What I liked about the old Socialist Party of America is that it made room for Socialist of all stripes from Marxist, who considered themselves scientific Socialist, to Christian Socialist, and to those who were some of both (both Marxist and faith based Socialist to one degree or another.)
            </p>
            <p>
             This allowed for the SPA to have a much wider base then it otherwise would have had. Mother Jones was both a Socialist and a Catholic, for example.

             <a href="/user/uid:144846">
              dharmasyd
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:166438">
              gulfgal98
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:94755">
              FishOutofWater
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:146420">
              maryabein
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:29894">
              kharma
             </a>
            </dd>
           </dl>
          </div>
          <div class="ct">
           <blockquote>
            Had I one wish for the churches of America, I think it would be that they come to see the difference between charity and justice.
            <p>
             Charity is a matter of personal attributes; justice is a matter of public policy. Charity seeks to alleviate the effects of injustice; justice seeks to eliminate the causes of it.
            </p>
            <p>
             Charity in no way affects the status quo, while justice leads inevitably to political confrontation. Especially I would hope that Christians would see that the compassion that moved the Good Samaritan to act charitably  that same compassion prompted Biblical prophets to confront injustice.
            </p>
            <p>
             Martin Luther King, Jr., better than any other public figure, understood the nature of compassion, that it does not exclude confrontation. It was his message that its not enough to suffer with the poor; we must confront the
             <br/>
             people and systems that cause poverty. It was Martins message that you cannot set the captive free if youre not willing to confront those who hold the keys.
            </p>
           </blockquote>
           William Sloan Coffin (Credo, p. 43)
           <p>
            And, it's not just the churches...it's all americans. That thousand points of light bullshit was nothing but a head fake to avoid doing anything about the real problems.
           </p>
          </div>
          <div class="cf">
           <p class="sig">
            The darkest places in hell are reserved for those who maintain their neutrality in times of moral crisis. - Dante Alighieri
           </p>
           <p class="cb">
            by
            <a href="/user/uid:78655">
             Persiflage
            </a>
            on
            <a href="/comments/1308997/53758723#c83">

            </a>
           </p>

        <li id="c109">
         <div class="cx" id="cx53760985">
          <h5>
           <a class="de">
           </a>
           <span class="cu">
            Exciting diary, OPOL.
           </span>
           <span class="crd ntb">
            (
            <a href="/comments/1308997/53760985#c109?mode=alone;showrate=1#c109">
             3+ / 0-
            </a>
            )
           </span>
          </h5>
          <div class="crs">
           <dl>
            <dt>
             Recommended by:
            </dt>
            <dd>
             <a href="/user/uid:29894">
              kharma
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:85446">
              One Pissed Off Liberal
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:321609">
              JayRaye
             </a>
            </dd>
           </dl>
          </div>
          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            We share a common goal- albeit in two entirely different ecosystems. If all goes according to plan, I should be officially establishing my own business founded on permaculture ethics this summer here in Finland.
           </p>
           <p>
            It always amazes me just how many people who are politically engaged, consider themselves progressive, and consider climate change to be the greatest threat facing humanity, are still unaware of the power that agroecology, agroforestry, and ecological design hold for a regenerative future. I've blogged about it, you've blogged about it, and many others have. The UN has come out very strongly in favor of these things and even the World Bank has funded large-scale projects. World Vision is promoting Farmer Managed Natural Regeneration with increasing velocity.
           </p>
           <p>
            I would think that by now it would be more appropriate if, each and every time we mention the threat of climate change or other environmental dangers (heck, even social ones), that we include some of the solutions.
           </p>
           <p>
            Too many stories read: problem, problem, problem- despair.
           </p>
           <p>
            Not enough read: problem, solution, action.
           </p>
           <p>
            Glad to see you are still around to write the latter.
           </p>
          </div>
          <div class="cf">

        <li id="c115">
         <div class="cx" id="cx53762780">
          <h5>
           <a class="de">
           </a>
           <span class="cu">
            One of the things that is clear to me is...
           </span>
           <span class="crd ntb">
            (
            <a href="/comments/1308997/53762780#c115?mode=alone;showrate=1#c115">
             4+ / 0-
            </a>
            )
           </span>
          </h5>
          <div class="crs">
           <dl>
            <dt>
             Recommended by:
            </dt>
            <dd>
             <a href="/user/uid:141635">
              greengemini
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:321609">
              JayRaye
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:85446">
              One Pissed Off Liberal
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:1008411">
              snwflk
             </a>
            </dd>
           </dl>
          </div>
          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            ...the asymmetry between the right and left.
           </p>
           <p>
            On the left we care about the downtrodden, the handicapped, the poor, the sick, the marginalized, etc. We are compassionate. We care about the future generations so we are committed to stop global warming and protecting the environment.
           </p>
           <p>
            We are involved in a thousand causes at the global, national and local level.
           </p>
           <p>
            On the right they are selfish (Ayn Rand wrote
            <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Virtue_of_Selfishness">
             The Virtue of Selfishness
            </a>
            after all) or in stopping abortion which they consider murder or in keeping racial minorities from achieving any political power. That is all. They also have the
            <a href="http://www.thenation.com/article/180267/exclusive-behind-koch-brothers-secret-billionaire-summit">
             Billionaires Boys Club
            </a>
            on their side, lead by the Koch bros.
           </p>
           <p>
            So things have to change or we are doomed.
           </p>
           <p>
            But we need to unite.
           </p>
           <p>
            This is one of the reasons why I support the money out of politics movement because as long as money can play the corrupting role it plays, all of our causes are prevented from succeeding.
           </p>
           <center>
            <br/>
            <img alt="Money out of politics photo Moneyoutofpolitics_zps782ff718.png" border="0" src="http://i97.photobucket.com/albums/l217/Shockwave_73/Album%202/Moneyoutofpolitics_zps782ff718.png"/>
            <br/>
           </center>
          </div>
          <div class="cf">
           <p class="sig">
            Daily Kos an oasis of truth. Truth that leads to action.
           </p>
           <p class="cb">
            by
            <a href="/user/uid:9742">
             Shockwave
            </a>
            on
            <a href="/comments/1308997/53762780#c115">

            </a>
           </p>
           <p class="cl">

        <li id="c128">
         <div class="cx" id="cx53765663">
          <h5>
           <a class="de">
           </a>
           <span class="cu">
            Compassionate conservatives. . .
           </span>
           <span class="crd ntb">
            (
            <a href="/comments/1308997/53765663#c128?mode=alone;showrate=1#c128">
             0+ / 0-
            </a>
            )
           </span>
          </h5>
          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            Oh, how easy it is to slide into stereotypical generalities! You say, "Apologies to compassionate conservatives,
            <strong>
             should there be any
            </strong>
            . . ."
            <br/>
            I know many. Yes, I can generalize and say that many "conservatives" do indeed subscribe to "I earned mine, it belongs to me, and I'm not sharing it with the likes of you." But many do not. Compassionate conservatives have trouble with the extreme libertarian view that nobody deserve any benefits that they cannot afford to provide for themselves. Many (I won't claim "all," but definitely
            <em>
             many
            </em>
            ) evangelical Christians recognize that the Bible does indeed command us to help the oppressed, and even to have compassion on the "failures" (alcoholics, drug addicts, etc.)
            <br/>
            If I can generalize the difference between "liberal" and "conservative" extremes, I would argue that conservative extremists seem to believe that
            <strong>
             all
            </strong>
            "failures" are due to personal character flaws, while liberal extremists seem to believe that
            <strong>
             no
            </strong>
            failures are the fault of the individual. Both of those extremes are mistaken. Sometimes the individual really is to blame, but other times he/she is not. So generalities should be avoided.
           </p>
           <p>
            Evan
           </p>
          </div>
          <div class="cf">
           <p class="sig">
           </p>

        <li id="c131">
         <div class="cx" id="cx53766180">
          <h5>
           <a class="de">
           </a>
           <span class="cu">
            I am an atheist Christian. HUH????
           </span>
           <span class="crd ntb">
            (
            <a href="/comments/1308997/53766180#c131?mode=alone;showrate=1#c131">
             3+ / 0-
            </a>
            )
           </span>
          </h5>
          <div class="crs">
           <dl>
            <dt>
             Recommended by:
            </dt>
            <dd>
             <a href="/user/uid:321609">
              JayRaye
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:85446">
              One Pissed Off Liberal
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:1008411">
              snwflk
             </a>
            </dd>
           </dl>
          </div>
          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            Jesus was a fantastic philosopher and many of the 'lessons' attributed to him are very humane and very humble. So they are attractive to me as a humanitarian. But I don't think there is a 'God' nor then do I believe he is/was the son of 'God' - anymore than I think Gandhi was. But as philosophers, they both rank pretty high on my internal scale.
           </p>
           <p>
            Just like the author, if that makes me a communist or a socialist, then I am very proud of that moniker and will wear it proudly. The right is NOT Christian - note the root of the word:
            <strong>
             CHRIST
            </strong>
            . They do not even attempt to adhere to his teachings: "Do unto others as you would have others do unto you"; "Let them who is without sin be the first to cast a stone"; "Judge not and ye shall not be judged"; "No man can know the will of God".
           </p>
           <p>
            That last one always gets them - How can you tell whether God is for or against anything? Aren't all these evangelists telling you they know? How would they know? They are men, aren't they?
           </p>
          </div>
          <div class="cf">
           <p class="sig">
           </p>
           <p class="cb">

            <a href="/user/uid:1002761">

        <ul class="cm i1" id="k53766180">
         <li id="c134">
          <div class="cx" id="cx53767227">
           <h5>
            <a class="de">
            </a>
            <span class="cu">
             You are *mostly* right
            </span>
            <span class="crd ntb">
             (
             <a href="/comments/1308997/53767227#c134?mode=alone;showrate=1#c134">
              1+ / 0-
             </a>
             )
            </span>
           </h5>
           <div class="crs">
            <dl>
             <dt>
              Recommended by:
             </dt>
             <dd>
              <a href="/user/uid:321609">
               JayRaye
              </a>
             </dd>
            </dl>
           </div>
           <div class="ct">
            <p>
             You got three out of four:
            </p>
            <p>
             "Do unto others as you would have others do unto you"
             <br/>
             (Thats in Matthew 7:12)
             <br/>
             "Let them who are without sin be the first to cast a stone"
             <br/>
             (Thats in John 8:7)
             <br/>
             "Judge not and ye shall not be judged"
             <br/>
             (Thats in Matthew 7:1)
             <br/>
             "No man can know the will of God"
             <br/>
             (That ones a 404, Not Found)
            </p>
            <p>
             Of course, that last thought depends on what you mean. In specific cases where a decision must be made, probably most Christians acknowledge that direct divine revelation cannot be assumed (though some, particularly Pentecostals, would disagree). But if you refer to generalities and accept the Bible as being a true guide (not all do, of course, but if one does. . .) then one can know the will of God in a general sense, such as Thou shalt not steal, Thou shalt not commit adultery, and so on. And one such general commandwell, actually twostate that Gods people should love their neighbors as they love their own selves (Leviticus 19:18) and that they should love the stranger who is among them as much as they should love any other (Leviticus 19:34).
             <br/>
             The bottom line is that if you disparage and attack Christians who take the Bible seriously, you may be driving away potential allies. Sure, some do not practice what they claim to believe (the Bible), but many sincerely try to. And that includes advocating the cause of the poor and oppressed.
            </p>
            <p>
             Evan
             <br/>
            </p>

          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            Thank you for articulating what has always been most important to me. I have fought constantly to elevate the discussion from singular issues to an awareness of our most necessary human gift; empathy.
            <br/>
            Once we are rid of our most rigid bonds, and dispel the illusion of money (it doesn't exist - we created it out of thin air) and the delusions of organized religion we will be free to feel that which is most natural to us - empathy for each other an for all living creatures.
            <br/>
            If this sounds like Socialism or some sort of Communism, that is just the result of a centuries old advertizing campaign. What I refer to here is a ethos based on all that is life affirming.
           </p>

            <div class="ct">
             <p>
              You have good thoughts and express them well. And I applaud your effort to spread them. As a formula for human survival of the coming catastrophe they are better than most. I suppose the Humanitarian Left are the people the Christian Bible's Mathew was thinking about in the verse about the meek inheriting the Earth.
              <br/>
              But your ideas fall short of a way to slow or mitigate the human suffering that awaits us in the rest of this century. I think we have a good sense of the roots of the problem we face. What is needed is a framework of strategy that goes beyond yet more hopeless reenactments of Les Miserables or the 1890's Ghost Dances of Native Americans.
              <br/>
              Keep in mind that it took 400 years after the death of Jesus for the Romans to get so fat, dumb and lazy that a gang of barbarians beat the tar out of them and another 1000 years before Western Civilization finally woke up.
              <br/>
              Fortunately for humanity the Romans didn't have their fingers on the trigger of planetary destruction as we have with all our modern technology.
              <br/>
              Are there viable answers? Can we change the innate behavior of humans enough to keep us from destroying ourselves?
              <br/>
              I hope so. For the sake of our children I hope we can change the legacy we are leaving them.
              <br/>
              Flatmotor
             </p>
            </div>

         <div class="hasTooltip">
          <a class="title" href="/story/2015/07/14/1401439/-Black-Kos-Tuesday-s-Chile">
           Black Kos, Tuesday's Chile
          </a>
         </div>
         <div class="tooltipContents qtip-style-dk4_large qtip-pos-br">
          Musings on forgiveness: The personal and the political
Commentary by Chitown Kev

forgiveness is a part of Black American life. otherwise we'd have all gone insane long ago. 
mallyroyal

Forgiveness.
         </div>

          <span class="by">

          </span>

  <script type="text/javascript">
   if($.cookie('meter_user') !== 'false') {
		if ($('#ePostButton').length &gt; 0) {
		  $('#ePostButton').click(function() { 
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Posted Comment', { 
		      repliedTo: $(this).parents('#eP').prevAll('.cb').children('a').first().html() 
		    });
		  });
		}
		
		if (!!document.location.pathname.match('activate') &amp;&amp; $('h1:contains("Welcome to Daily Kos!")').length &gt; 0) {
		  DailyKos.Metrics.track('Signed Up');
		}
		
		if (document.location.pathname === '/') {
		  if (document.location.hostname.match(/^www|^dailykos/)) {
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Front Page');
		  } else {
		    var subdomain = document.location.hostname.split('.')[0];
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Vertical', { name: subdomain });
		  }
		}
		
		if ($('.ratinate').length &gt; 0) {
		  $('.ratinate').click(function() { DailyKos.Metrics.track('Recommended Comment') });
		}
		
		if ($('.do-addRating.type-story').length &gt; 0) {
		  $('.do-addRating.type-story').click(function() { DailyKos.Metrics.track('Recommended Story') });
		}
		
		if ($("form[action$='publishHow']").length &gt; 0) {
		  $(document).ready(function() {
			  $('.type-story.do-publishHow').click(function() { DailyKos.Metrics.track('Published Story') });
			 });
		}
		
		if (document.location.pathname.match(/^\/user/) &amp;&amp; $('li.here').length &gt; 0) {
		  if ($('.pageMenu:first li.here').children('a').html().match(/Stream/)) {
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Stream', { name: $('.name').children('a').html() });
		  } else if ($('.pageMenu:first li.here').children('a').html().match(/Profile/)) {
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Profile', { name: $('.name').children('a').html() });
		  } else if ($('.pageMenu:last li.here').children('a').html().match(/My Recent Replies/)) {
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Replies');
		  }
		} 
		
		if ($('#search-tabbed').length &gt; 0) {
		  DailyKos.Metrics.track('Searched');
		}
		
		if ($('#group-tables').length &gt; 0) {
			DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Groups List');
		}
		
		if (document.location.pathname.match(/^\/groups/) &amp;&amp; $("#group_info").length &gt; 0) {
		  DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Group', { name: $('.name').children('a').text() });
		}
		
		if ($('.do-hotlist.type-user, .do-unHotlist.type-user').length &gt; 0) {
		  $('.do-hotlist.type-user, .do-unHotlist.type-user').click(function() {
		    var nickName;
		    nickName = ($(this).prev('a').html() || $('.name a').html())
		    if ($(this).hasClass('do-hotlist')) {
		      DailyKos.Metrics.track('Followed User', { nickname: nickName }) 
		    } else if ($(this).hasClass('do-unHotlist')) {
		      DailyKos.Metrics.track('Unfollowed User', { nickname: nickName }) 
		    }    
		  });
		}
	}
  </script>
